--- Commit Message ---
LU-14428 libcfs: replace tracefile buffer with ring_buffer

Linux has a generic ring-buffer API which uses minimal locking and
allows entries to be appended from any context.  This is essentially
the same functionality provided by trace_data abstraction in
tracefile.c, though with less locking overhead.

This patch removes the trace_data support and switches to use
ring_buffer.

The API functionality is not identical so some adjustments need to be
made.  In particular once an entry in the log has been reserved, it is
not possible to reduce the size of the reservation, only to use it or
discard it, where discarding might result in the space being wasted in
the rare case that more space is reserved from a different context
(e.g.  interrupt).

So instead we use a modest sized on-stack buffer to hold the formatted
result, and strcpy() that to a ring_buffer.  If the on-stack buffer
isn't big enough (approximately 20% of messages in some testings) we
need to format a second time, though we do that less often than the
current code.  The strcpy should be fast compared to vsprintf so this
should be a net win.

ring_buffer doesn't record whether a message was generated in
interrupt or process context and the information is not generally
useful, so that field in the ptldebug_header is now always set to
zero.

The pages stored in ring_buffer are not the same format as are
expected by user-space, so we cannot extract whole pages and copy them
to the file, but instead extract individual entries and write them to
the file.

Similarly, pages cannot be moved to the daemon_list, but the contents
need to be copied.

Also discard libcfs_debug_binary as it is ALWAYS 1 and the code would
be buggy if it were zero.

Signed-off-by: Mr NeilBrown <neilb@suse.de>

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-07-05 11:50:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19:

The earlier bug which resulted in trace lines going missing was deceptively simply.
The API for creating a ring_buffer was the size in byte (for each per-cpu buffer).
I was providing the size if pages (incorrectly multiplied by the number of cpus).
So the buffer was tiny an easily overflowed.

It seems to work now.  Any feeling game to review this for me?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-07-06 19:23:19.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19: Code-Review+1

It looks reasonable.  There is an open question about whether the performance is better or worse than before, but the LOC is certainly down (-600) so that is a win.

Having a new userspace interface to the "debug_daemon" (continuous logging) functionality would also be useful, and likely a CPU reduction from converting all of the debug messages twice.

Bonus would be if regular users could somehow access a subset of the trace logs (e.g. rpctrace, dlmtrace, vfstrace, malloc) that are under their PID/UID, since there have been several requests over the years to add this kind of information to application profiling tools, but it is behind the "kernel/root only" paywall right now.

I haven't looked into this in any detail, just putting it out there if you have some experience in this area.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-07-09 12:53:38.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19: Code-Review+1

Thanks for finding the bug.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-07-11 18:21:02.000000000) ---

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2023-07-19 04:55:11.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19:

ugh, the description states taht all formattign is expected to run twice.

We had to severely limit default logging because of how slow it was otherwise and everybody cries today how slow the system becomes when we ask them for elevated debug, and this seemignly will make everything even slower?

Can we, I dunno, have local buffer where we'd run the formatting just once and copy out of there after a succesful allocation or some such? Still slower than a single formatting pass I guess.

We'll definitely need to run some tests with say debug level set to -1 to see what happens compared to today.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-07-19 05:41:07.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19:

> Patch Set 19:
> 
> ugh, the description states taht all formattign is expected to run twice.

To be precise: the current code runs the formatting twice if the message is longer than 85 chars.  The current patch does if it is longer than 40.  So yes: it will run twice more often.

> Can we, I dunno, have local buffer where we'd run the formatting just once and copy out of there after a succesful allocation or some such? Still slower than a single formatting pass I guess.

I guess a strcpy is a lot faster than sprintf, so that would be faster.
We should be able to afford a 100byte on-stack buffer.  The kernel has a big stack these days.
Then we would only need a second run when the message is longer than that.

I'll look at some debug logs and see where the sweet-spot is.

Thanks.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-07-19 06:06:55.000000000) ---
Patch Set 19:

> I'll look at some debug logs and see where the sweet-spot is.

Having looked at one random sample, over half are under 44 chars, 3/4 are under 75.
There is a gap between 182 and 256 - nothing of that length.  14% are more than 200.

100 looks good.  Only 20% would need to run the formatting twice.  On my one sample set anyway.

--- Message (Alex Zhuravlev, 2023-09-19 18:04:25.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

is there an extention to crash tool to extract data from ring buffers?

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-09-20 00:16:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

> Patch Set 21:
> 
> is there an extention to crash tool to extract data from ring buffers?

https://github.com/fujitsu/crash-trace 
contains an extension to "crash" for extracting ftrace information which is also stored in a ring_buffer.  Possibly it can be used as-is, or else it likely wouldn't be too hard to extend it to extract the lustre-debug ring_buffer.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-09-20 21:50:33.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

Also see this thread:

http://lists.lustre.org/pipermail/lustre-devel-lustre.org/2023-July/011041.html

--- Message (Oleg Drokin, 2023-09-25 07:19:59.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

(1 comment)

seems to have something strange goign on with long lines (?) at times as if there's some sort of a calculation error for the string size or some such.

--- Message (Neil Brown, 2023-09-27 00:31:19.000000000) ---
Patch Set 21:

The only explanation I can think of is that sometimes the second call to vsprintf - when the buffer provided is large enough - returns a slightly smaller result.  i.e. when it doesn't have buffer space to complete the formatting, maybe it estimates a little high sometimes ???
If that happened, the old code would cope and the new code would not.
This is because the new code assumes the result will be the same and so doesn't look at the return value from the second vsnprintf call.  I will fix that.

--- Message (Timothy Day, 2023-10-26 23:33:40.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

Perhaps naive idea: why not dump all of the Lustre debugging info into /sys/kernel/tracing/trace by redefining CDEBUG and friends using trace_printk()? I tested the idea myself. The log output looks pretty similar. Performance/CPU didn't seem worse (although that would need more extensive testing). The conversion would be pretty simple and we'd still benefit from a lot of the advanced kernel tracing features. And we could retain many of the custom Lustre debugging features.

I'm not sure how happy upstream kernel would be with that approach. Although, I doubt they like custom debugging either. We could just disable the tracing by default in upstream client. I saw some drivers upstream kind of do something similar (drivers/gpu/drm/i915/i915_gem.h has a bunch of custom macros using trace_printk()).

`lctl debug_kernel` and such could be refactored to read from /sys/kernel/tracing/trace and produce identical output. We could even borrow code from `trace_cmd` (also GPLv2). And we could still experiment with tracepoints later on.

Is there any obvious reason why this is a bad idea?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-10-27 02:28:02.000000000) ---
Patch Set 23:

> Perhaps naive idea: why not dump all of the Lustre debugging info
 > into /sys/kernel/tracing/trace by redefining CDEBUG and friends
 > using trace_printk()?

That is essentially what I had originally wanted - some easy mapping of CDEBUG messages to tracepoints, but if you look at patch https://review.whamcloud.com/24554 (last few comments and libcfs_trace.h) it ended up with about 40 LOC for every message, which would be a development nightmare.

If we can use trace_printk() instead of libcfs_debug_msg() as the underlying infrastructure for CDEBUG(), then that would be *much* less intrusive to the code and development process, and *reduces* LOC instead of increasing LOC.  I'm totally willing to move forward, but not go backward in terms of functionality or performance.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2024-01-17 21:56:25.000000000) ---
Patch Set 29: Code-Review+1

I'm going to optimistically mark this +1 so that it can make progress and be included into 2.16.  We need some improvements to the debug logging on systems with hundreds of cores, since having a per-core debug buffer size limit constrains those cores with active Lustre threads to flush logs quickly, and retains ancient logs for days.

It would be nice to get a second patch that optimizes the log handling so that they don't need to get processed twice.  I don't think we need userspace compatibility for very long, since the tools are almost always matching the kernel modules, but if we could get the _start_ of a new lctl interface into 2.16.0 (i.e. direct ringbuffer API) then we could decide the interop window separately.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2024-01-18 21:32:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 29:

Thank you Andreas for supporting this work. I do love your idea for supporting the new format with lctl and I do plan on working on it. Also Thomas didn't you want to do some kind of work along this line?

--- Message (Thomas Bertschinger, 2024-01-19 14:24:16.000000000) ---
Patch Set 29:

@james, yeah, I was interested in this. Unfortunately I haven't looked into this change in any detail yet, been way too busy with other things at LANL lately...
For the new mentioned lctl API, I don't know what that is planned to look like, but what I'd really like would be the ability to follow the log in real time.

I use the "-w" flag to dmesg basically every time I run dmesg, and it makes it way easier to debug issues without having to re-run dmesg after every single operation. 

On production clusters the flood of information might be too much for "lctl dk -w" to be very usable (at least without turning off most of the debug categories), but I could see it being really handy on development clusters.

What do you think, can a new userspace API support this?
